class="infobox-label">Current&#160;status</th><td class="infobox-data category">Active</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Yahoo!</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\xcb\x88</span><span title="/j/: &#39;y&#39; in &#39;yes&#39;">j</span><span title="/\xc9\x91\xcb\x90/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;father&#39;">\xc9\x91\xcb\x90</span><span title="&#39;h&#39; in &#39;hi&#39;">h</span><span title="/u\xcb\x90/: &#39;oo&#39; in &#39;goose&#39;">u\xcb\x90</span></span>/</a></span></span>, styled as <b>yahoo<i>!</i></b>)<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> is an American <a href="/wiki/Web_services" class="mw-redirect" title="Web services">web services</a> provider. It is headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Sunnyvale,_California" title="Sunnyvale, California">Sunnyvale, California</a> and is owned by <a href="/wiki/Verizon_Media" title="Verizon Media">Verizon Media</a>, pending sale to <a href="/wiki/Investment_fund" title="Investment fund">investment funds</a> managed by <a href="/wiki/Apollo_Global_Management" title="Apollo Global Management">Apollo Global Management</a>.\n</p><p>It provides a <a href="/wiki/Web_portal" title="Web portal">web portal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Search_engine" title="Search engine">search engine</a> <a href="/wiki/Yahoo!_Search" title="Yahoo! Search">Yahoo! Search</a>, and related services, including <a href="/wiki/My_Yahoo!" title="My Yahoo!">My Yahoo!</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yahoo!_Mail" title="Yahoo! Mail">Yahoo! Mail</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yahoo!_News" title="Yahoo! News">Yahoo! News</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yahoo!_Finance" title="Yahoo! Finance">Yahoo! Finance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yahoo_Sports" title="Yahoo Sports">Yahoo Sports</a> and its advertising platform, <a href="/wiki/Verizon_Media_Native" title="Verizon Media Native">Verizon Media Native</a>.\n</p><p>Yahoo! was established by <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Yang" title="Jerry Yang">Jerry Yang</a> and <a href="/wiki/David_Filo" title="David Filo">David Filo</a> in January 1994 and was one of the pioneers of the early Internet era in the 1990s.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> In 2000, it was the most popular website worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Usage declined as it lost market share to <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-telegraph.co.uk_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph.co.uk-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> However, Yahoo domain websites are still among the most popular websites, ranking 11th in global engagement according to both <a href="/wiki/Alexa_Internet" title="Alexa Internet">Alexa Internet</a><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/SimilarWeb" title="SimilarWeb">SimilarWeb</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" tocsection-12"><a href="#Scanning_emails_on_behalf_of_U.S._government"><span class="tocnumber">3.5</span> <span class="toctext">Scanning emails on behalf of U.S. government</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-13"><a href="#Allowing_French_citizens_to_purchase_Nazi_Party_paraphenalia"><span class="tocnumber">3.6</span> <span class="toctext">Allowing French citizens to purchase Nazi Party paraphenalia</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-14"><a href="#Paid_inclusion_in_Yahoo!_Search"><span class="tocnumber">3.7</span> <span class="toctext">Paid inclusion in Yahoo! Search</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-15"><a href="#Spyware_ads"><span class="tocnumber">3.8</span> <span class="toctext">Spyware ads</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-16"><a href="#Cooperation_with_Chinese_government"><span class="tocnumber">3.9</span> <span class="toctext">Cooperation with Chinese government</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-17"><a href="#Enabling_sexual_predators"><span class="tocnumber">3.10</span> <span class="toctext">Enabling sexual predators</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-18"><a href="#Connection_to_shark_fin_sales_via_previous_investment_in_Alibaba"><span class="tocnumber">3.11</span> <span class="toctext">Connection to shark fin sales via previous investment in Alibaba</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-19"><a href="#DMCA_notice_to_whistleblower"><span class="tocnumber">3.12</span> <span class="toctext">DMCA notice to whistleblower</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-20"><a href="#Censorship_of_private_emails_affiliated_with_Occupy_Wall_Street_protests"><span class="tocnumber">3.13</span> <span class="toctext">Censorship of private emails affiliated with Occupy Wall Street protests</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-21"><a href="#Participation_in_PRISM_surveillance_program"><span class="tocnumber">3.14</span> <span class="toctext">Participation in PRISM surveillance program</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-22"><a href="#Paradise_Papers"><span class="tocnumber">3.15</span> <span class="toctext">Paradise Papers</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-23"><a href="#Logos_and_themes"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Logos and themes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-24"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-25"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-26"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Yahoo!" title="History of Yahoo!">History of Yahoo!</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Yahoo!" title="Timeline of Yahoo!">Timeline of Yahoo!</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:DUBLIN_PRIDE_2015_(_YAHOO!_WERE_THERE_-_WERE_YOU%3F)-106289_(19257385102).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Yahoo_Portals_in_the_World.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Yahoo_Portals_in_the_World.JPG/300px-Yahoo_Portals_in_the_World.JPG" decoding="async" width="300" height="139" class="thumbimage" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Yahoo_Portals_in_the_World.JPG/600px-Yahoo_Portals_in_the_World.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1357" data-file-height="628" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Yahoo_Portals_in_the_World.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map showing localized versions of Yahoo! web portals, as of 2008</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Yahoo!_(4855962154).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Yahoo%21_%284855962154%29.jpg/170px-Yahoo%21_%284855962154%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="254" class="thumbimage" class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Yahoo!_(4855962154).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Yahoo sign at <a href="/wiki/Times_Square" title="Times Square">Times Square</a></div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Founding">Founding</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jerry_Yang_and_David_Filo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Jerry_Yang_and_David_Filo.jpg/220px-Jerry_Yang_and_David_Filo.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Jerry_Yang_and_David_Filo.jpg/330px-Jerry_Yang_and_David_Filo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Jerry_Yang_and_David_Filo.jpg/440px-Jerry_Yang_and_David_Filo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="899" data-file-height="677" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jerry_Yang_and_David_Filo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Jerry_Yang" title="Jerry Yang">Jerry Yang</a> and <a href="/wiki/David_Filo" title="David Filo">David Filo</a>, the founders of Yahoo</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Yahoo_screenshot_1994.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/34/Yahoo_screenshot_1994.png/220px-Yahoo_screenshot_1994.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="191" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/3/34/Yahoo_screenshot_1994.png 1.5x" data-file-width="324" data-file-height="282" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Yahoo_screenshot_1994.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Yahoo home page in 1994, when it was a directory. A <a href="/wiki/Search_engine" title="Search engine">search engine</a> was added in 1995.</div></div></div>\n<p>In January 1994, Yang and Filo were electrical engineering graduate students at <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University" title="Stanford University">Stanford University</a>, when they created a website named "Jerry and David\'s guide to the World Wide Web".<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> The site was a human-edited <a href="/wiki/Web_directory" title="Web directory">web directory</a>, organized in a hierarchy, as opposed to a searchable index of pages. In March 1994, "Jerry and David\'s Guide to the World Wide Web" was renamed "Yahoo!" and became known as the <a href="/wiki/Yahoo!_Directory" title="Yahoo! Directory">Yahoo! Directory</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Directory_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Directory-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> The "yahoo.com" domain was registered on January 18, 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The word "yahoo" is a <a href="/wiki/Backronym" title="Backronym">backronym</a> for "<a href="/wiki/Yet_another" title="Yet another">Yet Another</a> Hierarchically Organized Oracle"<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> or "Yet Another Hierarchical Officious Oracle".<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> The term "hierarchical" described how the Yahoo database was arranged in layers of subcategories. The term "oracle" was intended to mean "source of truth and wisdom", and the term "officious", rather than being related to the word\'s normal meaning, described the many office workers who would use the Yahoo database while surfing from work.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> However, Filo and Yang insist they mainly selected the name because they liked the slang definition of a "yahoo" (used by college students in David Filo\'s native Louisiana in the late 1980s and early 1990s to refer to an unsophisticated, rural Southerner): "rude, unsophisticated, uncouth."<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> This meaning derives from the <a href="/wiki/Yahoo_(Gulliver%27s_Travels)" title="Yahoo (Gulliver&#39;s Travels)">Yahoo</a> race of fictional beings from <i><a href="/wiki/Gulliver%27s_Travels" title="Gulliver&#39;s Travels">Gulliver\'s Travels</a></i>.\n</p><p>Yahoo! was incorporated on March 2, 1995. In 1995, a <a href="/wiki/Search_engine" title="Search engine">search engine</a> function, called <a href="/wiki/Yahoo!_Search" title="Yahoo! Search">Yahoo! Search</a>, was introduced. This allowed users to search Yahoo! Directory.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Yahoo soon became the first popular online directory and search engine on the <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Web" title="World Wide Web">World Wide Web</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Expansion">Expansion</span></h3>\n<p>Yahoo grew rapidly throughout the 1990s. Yahoo became a <a href="/wiki/Public_company" title="Public company">public company</a> via an <a href="/wiki/Initial_public_offering" title="Initial public offering">initial public offering</a> in April 1996 and its stock price rose 600% within two years.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Like many search engines and web directories, Yahoo added a web portal, putting it in competition with services including <a href="/wiki/Excite" title="Excite">Excite</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lycos" title="Lycos">Lycos</a>, and <a href="/wiki/America_Online" class="mw-redirect" title="America Online">America Online</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> By 1998, Yahoo was the most popular starting point for web users,<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> and the human-edited Yahoo Directory the most popular search engine,<sup id="cite_ref-Directory_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Directory-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> receiving 95 million page views per day, triple that of rival Excite.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> It also made many high-profile acquisitions. Yahoo began offering free <a href="/wiki/E-mail" class="mw-redirect" title="E-mail">e-mail</a> from October 1997 after the acquisition of <a href="/wiki/RocketMail" title="RocketMail">RocketMail</a>, which was then renamed to <a href="/wiki/Yahoo!_Mail" title="Yahoo! Mail">Yahoo! Mail</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> In 1998, Yahoo replaced <a href="/wiki/AltaVista" title="AltaVista">AltaVista</a> as the crawler-based search engine underlying the Directory with <a href="/wiki/Inktomi" title="Inktomi">Inktomi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Yahoo\'s two biggest acquisitions were made in 1999: <a href="/wiki/Geocities" class="mw-redirect" title="Geocities">Geocities</a> for $3.6 billion<sup id="cite_ref-buysgeo_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-buysgeo-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Broadcast.com" title="Broadcast.com">Broadcast.com</a> for $5.7 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Its stock price skyrocketed during the <a href="/wiki/Dot-com_bubble" title="Dot-com bubble">dot-com bubble</a>, closing at an all-time high of $118.75/share on January 3, 2000. However, after the dot-com bubble burst, it reached a post-bubble low of $8.11 on September 26, 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:YAHOO_headquarters.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/YAHOO_headquarters.jpg/220px-YAHOO_headquarters.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/YAHOO_headquarters.jpg/330px-YAHOO_headquarters.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/YAHOO_headquarters.jpg/440px-YAHOO_headquarters.jpg 2x" data-file-width="480" data-file-height="361" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:YAHOO_headquarters.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Yahoo headquarters in 2001</div></div></div>\n<p>Yahoo began using <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a> for search in June 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Over the next four years, it developed its own search technologies, which it began using in 2004 partly using technology from its $280 million acquisition of Inktomi in 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> In response to Google\'s <a href="/wiki/Gmail" title="Gmail">Gmail</a>, Yahoo began to offer unlimited email storage in 2007. In 2008, the company laid off hundreds of people as it struggled from competition.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In February 2008, <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a> made an unsolicited bid to acquire Yahoo! for $44.6 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Yahoo!-Inc-Feb-2008-425_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yahoo!-Inc-Feb-2008-425-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Yahoo rejected the bid, claiming that it "substantially undervalues" the company and was not in the interest of its shareholders. Although Microsoft increased its bid to $47 billion, Yahoo insisted on another 10%+ increase to the offer and Microsoft cancelled the offer in May 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Yahoo!-Inc-May-2008-8-K_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yahoo!-Inc-May-2008-8-K-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Yahoo!-Inc-Jun-2008-8-K_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yahoo!-Inc-Jun-2008-8-K-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Carol_Bartz" title="Carol Bartz">Carol Bartz</a>, who had no previous experience in Internet advertising replaced Yang as CEO in January 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-Yahoo!-Inc-Jan-2009-8-K_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yahoo!-Inc-Jan-2009-8-K-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> In September 2011, after failing to meet targets, she was fired by chairman <a href="/wiki/Roy_J._Bostock" title="Roy J. Bostock">Roy J. Bostock</a>; CFO <a href="/wiki/Tim_Morse" title="Tim Morse">Tim Morse</a> was named as Interim CEO of the company.<sup id="cite_ref-Yahoo!-Inc-Sep-2011-8-K_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yahoo!-Inc-Sep-2011-8-K-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In April 2012, after the appointment of <a href="/wiki/Scott_Thompson_(businessman)" title="Scott Thompson (businessman)">Scott Thompson</a> as CEO, several key executives resigned, including <a href="/wiki/Chief_product_officer" title="Chief product officer">chief product officer</a> <a href="/wiki/Blake_Irving" title="Blake Irving">Blake Irving</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Yahoo!-Inc-Apr-2012-10-K/A_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yahoo!-Inc-Apr-2012-10-K/A-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> On April 4, 2012, Yahoo announced 2,000 layoffs,<sup id="cite_ref-Yahoo!-Inc-Apr-2012-8-K_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yahoo!-Inc-Apr-2012-8-K-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> or about 14% of its 14,100 workers by the end of year, expected to save around $375 million annually.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> In an email sent to employees in April 2012, Thompson reiterated his view that customers should come first at Yahoo. He also completely reorganized the company.<sup id="cite_ref-Swisher_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Swisher-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On May 13, 2012, Thompson was fired and was replaced on an interim basis by <a href="/wiki/Ross_Levinsohn" title="Ross Levinsohn">Ross Levinsohn</a>, recently appointed head of Yahoo\'s new Media group. Several associates of <a href="/wiki/Third_Point_Management" title="Third Point Management">Third Point Management</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Daniel_S._Loeb" title="Daniel S. Loeb">Daniel S. Loeb</a> were nominated to the <a href="/wiki/Board_of_directors" title="Board of directors">board of directors</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Yahoo!-Inc-May-2012-8-K_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yahoo!-Inc-May-2012-8-K-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Swisher_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Swisher-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> Thompson\'s total compensation for his 130-day tenure with Yahoo was at least $7.3 million.<sup id="cite_ref-CNN_ousted_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNN_ousted-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On July 15, 2012, <a href="/wiki/Marissa_Mayer" title="Marissa Mayer">Marissa Mayer</a> was appointed president and CEO of Yahoo, effective July 17, 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-Yahoo!-Inc-Jul-2012-8-K_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yahoo!-Inc-Jul-2012-8-K-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In June 2013, Yahoo acquired <a href="/wiki/Blog" title="Blog">blogging</a> site <a href="/wiki/Tumblr" title="Tumblr">Tumblr</a> for $1.1 billion in cash, with Tumblr\'s CEO and founder <a href="/wiki/David_Karp" title="David Karp">David Karp</a> continuing to run the site.<sup id="cite_ref-Yahoo!-Inc-Jun-2013-8-K_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yahoo!-Inc-Jun-2013-8-K-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Yahoo!-Inc-May-2013-8-K_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yahoo!-Inc-May-2013-8-K-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> In July 2013, Yahoo! announced plans to open an office in San Francisco.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On August 2, 2013, Yahoo acquired <a href="/wiki/Rockmelt" title="Rockmelt">Rockmelt</a>; its staff was retained, but all of its existing products were terminated.<sup id="cite_ref-tc-rockmelt_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tc-rockmelt-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Data collated by comScore during July 2013 revealed that, during the month, more people in the U.S. visited Yahoo websites than Google; the first time that Yahoo outperformed Google since 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> The data did not count mobile usage, nor Tumblr.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Mayer also hired <a href="/wiki/Katie_Couric" title="Katie Couric">Katie Couric</a> to be the anchor of a new online news operation and started an online food magazine. However, by January 2014, doubts of her progress emerged when she fired her first major hire, Henrique de Castro.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On December 12, 2014, Yahoo acquired <a href="/wiki/Video_advertising" title="Video advertising">video advertising</a> provider <a href="/wiki/BrightRoll" title="BrightRoll">BrightRoll</a> for $583 million.<sup id="cite_ref-Yahoo!-Inc-Feb-2015-10-K_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yahoo!-Inc-Feb-2015-10-K-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On November 21, 2014, Yahoo acquired <a href="/wiki/Cooliris" title="Cooliris">Cooliris</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Decline.2C_security_breaches.2C_and_sale"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Decline,_security_breaches,_and_sale">Decline, security breaches, and sale</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Yahoo!_data_breaches" title="Yahoo! data breaches">Yahoo! data breaches</a></div>\n<p>By December 2015, Mayer was criticized as performance declined.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> Mayer was ranked as the least likable CEO in tech.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On February 2, 2016, Mayer announced layoffs amounting to 15% of the Yahoo! workforce.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On July 25, 2016, <a href="/wiki/Verizon_Communications" title="Verizon Communications">Verizon Communications</a> announced the acquisition of Yahoo\'s core Internet business for $4.83 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-Yahoo!-Inc-Jul-2016-8-K_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yahoo!-Inc-Jul-2016-8-K-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> The deal excluded Yahoo\'s 15% stake in <a href="/wiki/Alibaba_Group" title="Alibaba Group">Alibaba Group</a> and 35.5% stake in <a href="/wiki/Yahoo!_Japan" title="Yahoo! Japan">Yahoo! Japan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Yahoo!-Inc-Aug-2016-DEFA14A_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yahoo!-Inc-Aug-2016-DEFA14A-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Yahoo!-Inc-Jul-2016-2-8-K_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yahoo!-Inc-Jul-2016-2-8-K-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On February 21, 2017, as a result of the <a href="/wiki/Yahoo!_data_breaches" title="Yahoo! data breaches">Yahoo! data breaches</a>, Verizon lowered its purchase price for Yahoo! by $350 million and reached an agreement to share liabilities regarding the data breaches.<sup id="cite_ref-bloomberg-lower_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bloomberg-lower-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-usatoday-verizonshaved_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usatoday-verizonshaved-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On June 13, 2017, Verizon completed the acquisition of Yahoo! and <a href="/wiki/Marissa_Mayer" title="Marissa Mayer">Marissa Mayer</a> resigned.<sup id="cite_ref-Altaba-Jun-2017-8-K_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Altaba-Jun-2017-8-K-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:0_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Yahoo!-Inc-Feb-2017-8-K_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yahoo!-Inc-Feb-2017-8-K-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Yahoo!-Inc-Jun-2017-SC-TO-I/A_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yahoo!-Inc-Jun-2017-SC-TO-I/A-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Yahoo!-Inc-May-2017-SC-TO-I_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yahoo!-Inc-May-2017-SC-TO-I-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Yahoo, AOL, and <a href="/wiki/HuffPost" title="HuffPost">HuffPost</a> were to continue operating under their own names, under the umbrella of a new company, Oath Inc., later called <a href="/wiki/Verizon_Media" title="Verizon Media">Verizon Media</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Yahoo!-Inc-Jul-2017-8-K_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yahoo!-Inc-Jul-2017-8-K-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-verge-oath_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-verge-oath-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The parts of the original Yahoo Inc. which were not purchased by <a href="/wiki/Verizon_Communications" title="Verizon Communications">Verizon Communications</a> were renamed <a href="/wiki/Altaba" title="Altaba">Altaba</a>, which liquidated, making a final distribution in October 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-Yahoo-Jun-2017-8-K_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yahoo-Jun-2017-8-K-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Altaba-Jun-2017-2-8-K_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Altaba-Jun-2017-2-8-K-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Yahoo!-Inc-May-2017-SC-TO-I_97-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yahoo!-Inc-May-2017-SC-TO-I-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Yahoo!-Inc-Jun-2017-N-2_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yahoo!-Inc-Jun-2017-N-2-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In May 2021, Verizon agreed to sell <a href="/wiki/Verizon_Media" title="Verizon Media">Verizon Media</a>, including Yahoo!, to <a href="/wiki/Investment_fund" title="Investment fund">investment funds</a> managed by <a href="/wiki/Apollo_Global_Management" title="Apollo Global Management">Apollo Global Management</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Chief_Executive_Officers">Chief Executive Officers</span></h3>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Marissa_Mayer" title="Marissa Mayer">Marissa Mayer</a> (2012\xe2\x80\x932017)<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Ross_Levinsohn" title="Ross Levinsohn">Ross Levinsohn</a> Interim (2012)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Scott_Thompson_(businessman)" title="Scott Thompson (businessman)">Scott Thompson</a> (2012)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Tim_Morse" title="Tim Morse">Tim Morse</a> Interim (2011\xe2\x80\x932012)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Carol_Bartz" title="Carol Bartz">Carol Bartz</a> (2009\xe2\x80\x932011)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Jerry_Yang" title="Jerry Yang">Jerry Yang</a> (2007\xe2\x80\x932009)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Terry_Semel" title="Terry Semel">Terry Semel</a> (2001\xe2\x80\x932007)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Timothy_Koogle" title="Timothy Koogle">Timothy Koogle</a> (1995\xe2\x80\x932001)</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Products_and_services">Products and services</span></h2>\n<p>For a list of all current and defunct services offered by Yahoo!, see <a href="/wiki/List_of_Yahoo!-owned_sites_and_services" title="List of Yahoo!-owned sites and services">List of Yahoo!-owned sites and services</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism">Criticism</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Criticism_of_Yahoo!" title="Criticism of Yahoo!">Criticism of Yahoo!</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Privacy">Privacy</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:DigiGes_PRISM05.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/DigiGes_PRISM05.jpg/220px-DigiGes_PRISM05.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/DigiGes_PRISM05.jpg/330px-DigiGes_PRISM05.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/DigiGes_PRISM05.jpg/440px-DigiGes_PRISM05.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:DigiGes_PRISM05.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Protest against the mass surveillance by the <a href="/wiki/National_Security_Agency" title="National Security Agency">NSA</a></div></div></div>\n<p>In September 2013, Yahoo\'s transparency report said the company received 29,000 requests for information about users from governments in the first six months of 2013. Over 12,000 of the requests came from the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In October 2013, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Post" title="The Washington Post">The Washington Post</a></i> reported that the U.S. National Security Agency intercepted communications between Yahoo\'s data centers, as part of a program named <a href="/wiki/Muscular_(surveillance_program)" class="mw-redirect" title="Muscular (surveillance program)">Muscular</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In late January 2014, Yahoo announced on its company blog that it had detected a "coordinated effort" to hack into possibly millions of Yahoo Mail accounts. The company prompted users to reset their passwords, but did not elaborate on the scope of the possible breach, citing an ongoing federal investigation.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In August 2015, researchers at <a href="/wiki/Malwarebytes" title="Malwarebytes">Malwarebytes</a>, notified Yahoo about its users getting hacked because of vulnerabilities in <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Flash_Player" title="Adobe Flash Player">Adobe Flash Player</a>. According to them, the <a href="/wiki/Vulnerability" title="Vulnerability">vulnerability</a> could allow attackers to install "ransomware" on users\' computers and lock their files until the customers pay the criminals.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Storing_personal_information_and_tracking_usage">Storing personal information and tracking usage</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Yahoo_Kimo_2008_Open_Hack_Day_stage_20080920.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Yahoo_Kimo_2008_Open_Hack_Day_stage_20080920.jpg/200px-Yahoo_Kimo_2008_Open_Hack_Day_stage_20080920.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Yahoo_Kimo_2008_Open_Hack_Day_stage_20080920.jpg/300px-Yahoo_Kimo_2008_Open_Hack_Day_stage_20080920.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Yahoo_Kimo_2008_Open_Hack_Day_stage_20080920.jpg/400px-Yahoo_Kimo_2008_Open_Hack_Day_stage_20080920.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1067" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Yahoo_Kimo_2008_Open_Hack_Day_stage_20080920.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Yahoo! Kimo (Taiwan) Open Hack Day event in 2008</div></div></div>\n<table class="box-Update plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="Ambox current red Americas.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Ambox_current_red_Americas.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red_Americas.svg.png" decoding="async" width="42" height="34" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Ambox_current_red_Americas.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red_Americas.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Ambox_current_red_Americas.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red_Americas.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="360" data-file-height="290" /></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section\'s <b><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute">factual accuracy</a> may be compromised due to out-of-date information</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">June 2012</span>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Working with comScore, in March 2008, <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> found that Yahoo was able to collect far more data about users than its competitors from its Web sites and advertising network. By one measure, on average Yahoo had the potential in December 2007 to build a profile of 2,500 records per month about each of its visitors, much more than <a href="/wiki/MySpace" class="mw-redirect" title="MySpace">MySpace</a>, <a href="/wiki/AOL" title="AOL">AOL</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> Yahoo retains search requests for a period of 13 months. However, in response to European regulators, Yahoo obfuscates the IP address of users after three months by deleting its last eight bits.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> Yahoo at the time had a 2-petabyte, specially built <a href="/wiki/Data_warehouse" title="Data warehouse">data warehouse</a> that it used to analyze the behavior of its users.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Do_Not_Track">Do Not Track</span></h3>\n<p>On March 29, 2012, Yahoo announced that it would introduce a "<a href="/wiki/Do_Not_Track" title="Do Not Track">Do Not Track</a>" feature that summer, allowing users to opt out of Web-visit tracking and customized advertisements.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> However, on April 30, 2014, Yahoo announced that it would no longer support the "Do Not Track" browser setting.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Data_breaches">Data breaches</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Yahoo!_data_breaches" title="Yahoo! data breaches">Yahoo! data breaches</a></div>\n<p>On September 22, 2016, Yahoo disclosed a <a href="/wiki/Data_breach" title="Data breach">data breach</a> that occurred in late 2014, in which information associated with at least 500 million user accounts,<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> one of the largest breaches reported to date.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> The United States indicted four men, including two employees of Russia\'s <a href="/wiki/Federal_Security_Service" title="Federal Security Service">Federal Security Service</a> (FSB), for their involvement in the hack.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> On December 14, 2016, the company revealed that another separate data breach had occurred in 2014, with hackers obtaining sensitive account information, including security questions, to at least one billion accounts.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> The company stated that hackers had utilized stolen internal software to forge <a href="/wiki/HTTP_cookie" title="HTTP cookie">HTTP cookies</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On October 3, 2017, the company stated that all 3 billion of its user accounts were affected by the August 2013 theft.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Scanning_emails_on_behalf_of_U.S._government">Scanning emails on behalf of U.S. government</span></h3>\n<p>In October 2016, Reuters reported that in 2015, Yahoo created software to search customers\' e-mail at the request of the <a href="/wiki/National_Security_Agency" title="National Security Agency">National Security Agency</a> or the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Bureau_of_Investigation" title="Federal Bureau of Investigation">Federal Bureau of Investigation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Allowing_French_citizens_to_purchase_Nazi_Party_paraphenalia">Allowing French citizens to purchase Nazi Party paraphenalia</span></h3>\n<p>In 2000, in the case of <i><a href="/wiki/LICRA_v._Yahoo!" title="LICRA v. Yahoo!">LICRA v. Yahoo!</a></i>, Yahoo was sued by parties seeking to prevent French citizens from purchasing memorabilia relating to the <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Party" title="Nazi Party">Nazi Party</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> In December 2001, Yahoo! asked a U.S. court to block the ruling.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> In August 2004, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Court_of_Appeals_for_the_Ninth_Circuit" title="United States Court of Appeals for the Ninth Circuit">United States Court of Appeals for the Ninth Circuit</a> ruled that it did not have jurisdiction over the matter.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> The decision was reversed in January 2006, and in May 2006, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Supreme_Court" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Supreme Court">United States Supreme Court</a> denied LICRA\'s request for <a href="/wiki/Certiorari" title="Certiorari">certiorari</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Paid_inclusion_in_Yahoo.21_Search"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Paid_inclusion_in_Yahoo!_Search">Paid inclusion in Yahoo! Search</span></h3>\n<p>In March 2004, Yahoo! launched a paid inclusion program whereby commercial websites were guaranteed listings on the Yahoo search engine.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> Yahoo discontinued the program at the end of 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Spyware_ads">Spyware ads</span></h3>\n<p>In May 2006, Yahoo! was sued in a <a href="/wiki/Class_action" title="Class action">class action</a> for providing ads via the Yahoo! ad network to companies who display them through <a href="/wiki/Spyware" title="Spyware">spyware</a> and <a href="/wiki/Adware" title="Adware">adware</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cooperation_with_Chinese_government">Cooperation with Chinese government</span></h3>\n<p>Yahoo, as well as other search engines, cooperated with the Chinese government on the <a href="/wiki/Great_Firewall" title="Great Firewall">Great Firewall</a>, supporting <a href="/wiki/Internet_censorship_in_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Internet censorship in the People&#39;s Republic of China">Internet censorship in the People\'s Republic of China</a>. In April 2005, dissident <a href="/wiki/Shi_Tao_(journalist)" title="Shi Tao (journalist)">Shi Tao</a> was sentenced to 10 years in prison for providing state secrets to foreign entities<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> as a result of being identified by IP address by Yahoo.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> Human rights organizations and the company\'s general counsel disputed the extent of Yahoo\'s foreknowledge of Shi\'s fate.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> Human rights groups also accuse Yahoo of aiding authorities in the arrest of dissidents <a href="/wiki/Li_Zhi_(dissident)" title="Li Zhi (dissident)">Li Zhi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jiang_Lijun" title="Jiang Lijun">Jiang Lijun</a>. In April 2017, Yahoo was sued for failing to uphold settlement agreements in this case. Yahoo pledged to give support to the families of those arrested and create a relief fund for those persecuted for expressing their views online with Yahoo Human Rights Trust. Of the $17.3 million allotted to this fund, $13 million had been used for a townhouse in Washington, DC and other purchases.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In September 2003, dissident <a href="/wiki/Wang_Xiaoning" title="Wang Xiaoning">Wang Xiaoning</a> was convicted of charges of "incitement to subvert state power" and was sentenced to ten years in prison. Yahoo Hong Kong connected Wang\'s group to a specific Yahoo e-mail address.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> Both Xiaoning\'s wife and the World Organization for Human Rights<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> sued Yahoo under human rights laws on behalf of Wang and Shi.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Enabling_sexual_predators">Enabling sexual predators</span></h3>\n<p>As a result of media scrutiny relating to Internet child predators and a lack of significant ad revenues, Yahoo\'s "user created" chatrooms were closed down in June 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> On May 25, 2006, Yahoo\'s image search was criticized for bringing up sexually explicit images even when <a href="/wiki/SafeSearch" title="SafeSearch">SafeSearch</a> was active.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Connection_to_shark_fin_sales_via_previous_investment_in_Alibaba">Connection to shark fin sales via previous investment in Alibaba</span></h3>\n<p>In August 2015, Yahoo acquired a 40% stake in <a href="/wiki/Alibaba_Group" title="Alibaba Group">Alibaba Group</a><sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> which was a subject of controversy for allowing the sale of shark-derived products. The company banned the sale of <a href="/wiki/Shark_fin_soup" title="Shark fin soup">shark fin</a> products on all its e-commerce platforms effective January 1, 2009.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="DMCA_notice_to_whistleblower">DMCA notice to whistleblower</span></h3>\n<p>On November 30, 2009, Yahoo was criticized by the <a href="/wiki/Electronic_Frontier_Foundation" title="Electronic Frontier Foundation">Electronic Frontier Foundation</a> for sending a <a href="/wiki/DMCA" class="mw-redirect" title="DMCA">DMCA</a> notice to <a href="/wiki/Whistleblower" title="Whistleblower">whistleblower</a> website "<a href="/wiki/Cryptome" title="Cryptome">Cryptome</a>" for publicly posting details, prices, and procedures on obtaining private information pertaining to Yahoo\'s subscribers.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Censorship_of_private_emails_affiliated_with_Occupy_Wall_Street_protests">Censorship of private emails affiliated with Occupy Wall Street protests</span></h3>\n<p>After some concerns over censorship of private emails regarding a website affiliated with <a href="/wiki/Occupy_Wall_Street" title="Occupy Wall Street">Occupy Wall Street</a> protests were raised, Yahoo responded with an apology and explained it as an accident.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-videosift.com_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-videosift.com-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-straight.com_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-straight.com-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Participation_in_PRISM_surveillance_program">Participation in PRISM surveillance program</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:PRISM_Collection_Details.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/PRISM_Collection_Details.jpg/220px-PRISM_Collection_Details.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/PRISM_Collection_Details.jpg/330px-PRISM_Collection_Details.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/PRISM_Collection_Details.jpg/440px-PRISM_Collection_Details.jpg 2x" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="525" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:PRISM_Collection_Details.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/PRISM_(surveillance_program)" title="PRISM (surveillance program)">PRISM</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Clandestine_operation" title="Clandestine operation">clandestine</a> <a href="/wiki/Global_surveillance" title="Global surveillance">global surveillance</a> program under which the <a href="/wiki/National_Security_Agency" title="National Security Agency">NSA</a> collects user data from companies like Yahoo.<sup id="cite_ref-bbcprism_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcprism-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>Following media reports about <a href="/wiki/PRISM_(surveillance_program)" title="PRISM (surveillance program)">PRISM</a>, NSA\'s massive electronic <a href="/wiki/Mass_surveillance" title="Mass surveillance">surveillance program</a>, in June 2013, several technology companies were identified as participants, including Yahoo.<sup id="cite_ref-bbcprism_167-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcprism-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Paradise_Papers">Paradise Papers</span></h3>\n<p>Yahoo is listed in the <a href="/wiki/Paradise_Papers" title="Paradise Papers">Paradise Papers</a>, a set of confidential electronic documents relating to <a href="/wiki/Offshore_investment" title="Offshore investment">offshore investment</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tax_avoidance" title="Tax avoidance">tax avoidance</a> that were leaked to the German newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/S%C3%BCddeutsche_Zeitung" title="S\xc3\xbcddeutsche Zeitung">S\xc3\xbcddeutsche Zeitung</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Logos_and_themes">Logos and themes</span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Yahoo!_icon_(2009-2013).svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Yahoo%21_icon_%282009-2013%29.svg/220px-Yahoo%21_icon_%282009-2013%29.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="127" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Yahoo%21_icon_%282009-2013%29.svg/330px-Yahoo%21_icon_%282009-2013%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Yahoo%21_icon_%282009-2013%29.svg/440px-Yahoo%21_icon_%282009-2013%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="577" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Yahoo!_icon_(2009-2013).svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Y!</i> moniker (2009\xe2\x80\x932013)</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Yahoo_701_First_Avenue.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Yahoo_701_First_Avenue.jpg/200px-Yahoo_701_First_Avenue.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="69" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Yahoo_701_First_Avenue.jpg/300px-Yahoo_701_First_Avenue.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Yahoo_701_First_Avenue.jpg/400px-Yahoo_701_First_Avenue.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="1031" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Yahoo_701_First_Avenue.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Yahoo sign with address at its headquarters</div></div></div>\n<p>The first Yahoo! logo was established upon foundation of the company in 2004. It consists of the "Yahoo" wordmark which is colored black and is using the <a href="/wiki/Times_New_Roman" title="Times New Roman">Times New Roman</a> font, but it was later changed.\n</p><p>In March 1995, when the company changed its name to Yahoo, it introduced another logo which is briefly changed to a more elaborate text that includes an exclamation point at the end.\n</p><p>In August 1995, Yahoo changed its logo to a stylized yellow jumping "Y" figurine on a blue circle while the "Yahoo!" wordmark is written below.\n</p><p>On January 1, 1996, Yahoo introduced a simplified new logo that included the text "Yahoo" and an exclamation mark, both in red with a slight shadow behind the text.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>By May 2009, Yahoo tweaked the logo by recoloring it from red to purple and removing the logo\'s outline and shadow. At the time, the purple logo was accompanied by a new slogan, "It\'s Y!ou." A shortened variant of the logo, consisting of only the letter "Y" and an exclamation point, was also used.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On August 7, 2013, at around midnight EDT, Yahoo announced that the final version of the new logo would be revealed on September 5, 2013 at 4:00&#160;a.m. UTC. In the period leading up to the unveiling of the new logo, the "30 Days of Change" campaign was introduced, whereby a variation of the logo was published every day for the 30 days following the announcement.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> The new logo was eventually launched with an accompanying video that showed its digital construction, and Mayer published a personalized description of the design process on her Tumblr page.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> Mayer explains:\n</p>\n<blockquote><p>So, one weekend this summer, I rolled up my sleeves and dove into the trenches with our logo design team ... We spent the majority of Saturday and Sunday designing the logo from start to finish, and we had a ton of fun weighing every minute detail. We knew we wanted a logo that reflected Yahoo \xe2\x80\x93 whimsical, yet sophisticated. Modern and fresh, with a nod to our history. Having a human touch, personal. Proud.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>\n<p>On September 19, 2013, Yahoo launched a new version of the "My Yahoo" personalized homepage. The redesign allows users to tailor a homepage with widgets that access features such as email accounts, calendars, Flickr and other Yahoo content, and Internet content. Users can also select "theme packs" that represent artists such as Polly Apfelbaum and Alec Monopoly, and bands such as <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_the_Sun_(band)" title="Empire of the Sun (band)">Empire of the Sun</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> Mayer then explained at a conference in late September 2013 that the logo change was the result of feedback from both external parties and employees.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In September 2019 Yahoo! changed its logo again for a "refreshed brand identity [that] is simpler and more flexible, and looks back to the original, quirky 1996 logo." The logo is a white text set against a purple background, with both the \xe2\x80\x9cy\xe2\x80\x9d and \xe2\x80\x9c!\xe2\x80\x9d of the logo reportedly set at an angle of 22.5 degrees. The logo was designed by <a href="/wiki/Pentagram_(design_firm)" title="Pentagram (design firm)">Pentagram</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:63.5px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Yahoo!_(2009-2013).svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Yahoo%21_%282009-2013%29.svg/120px-Yahoo%21_%282009-2013%29.svg.png" decoding="async" width="120" height="23" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Yahoo%21_%282009-2013%29.svg/180px-Yahoo%21_%282009-2013%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Yahoo%21_%282009-2013%29.svg/240px-Yahoo%21_%282009-2013%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="190" /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p><a href="/wiki/Wordmark" title="Wordmark">Wordmark</a> used from January 1, 1996 to September 4, 2013 (shown: purple variant used from 2009); red version still used by <a href="/wiki/Yahoo!_Japan" title="Yahoo! Japan">Yahoo! Japan</a>\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:61px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Yahoo!_(2013-2019).svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Yahoo%21_%282013-2019%29.svg/120px-Yahoo%21_%282013-2019%29.svg.png" decoding="async" width="120" height="28" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Yahoo%21_%282013-2019%29.svg/180px-Yahoo%21_%282013-2019%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Yahoo%21_%282013-2019%29.svg/240px-Yahoo%21_%282013-2019%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="121" /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p>Yahoo\'s fifth and previous logo, September 2013\xe2\x80\x93September 2019\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:58.5px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Yahoo!_(2019).svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Yahoo%21_%282019%29.svg/120px-Yahoo%21_%282019%29.svg.png" decoding="async" width="120" height="33" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Yahoo%21_%282019%29.svg/180px-Yahoo%21_%282019%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Yahoo%21_%282019%29.svg/240px-Yahoo%21_%282019%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="277" /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p>Yahoo\'s sixth and current logo, September 2019\xe2\x80\x93present\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n</ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span></h2>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/List_of_search_engines" title="List of search engines">List of search engines</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Yahoo!_litigation" title="Yahoo! litigation">Yahoo! litigation</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span></h2>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style><div class="reflist">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap mw-references-columns"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-Yahoo!-Inc-Mar-2017-10-K-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Yahoo!-Inc-Mar-2017-10-K_1-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"/><cite class="citation web cs1"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://edgar.secdatabase.com/2179/119312517065791/filing-main.htm">"Yahoo!
